## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time derivative of population size P, indicating a dynamical systems/ODE setting where growth depends on current population (density dependence) and possibly explicit time forcing (seasonality, interventions). Typical models express dP_dt as a function of P alone or of both t and P.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate in unlimited resources)
- Linear source-sink with baseline: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (immigration/emigration or stocking independent of P)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slowly changing environment over time)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita rate)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent limitation; carrying capacity encoded by c1)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (generalized density dependence; c2 shapes approach to carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (growth slows roughly logarithmically with size; c1 sets scale)
- Richards-type growth (flexible sigmoid in ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) * (c3 + (c1 * P) ** c2) (extra shape flexibility for asymmetric sigmoids)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (negative growth at low P; depensation)
- Allee effect (weak) with saturating term: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P) / (1 + c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P without mandatory extinction threshold)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant-yield removal/harvest)
- Logistic with proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (effort proportional to population)
- Saturating per-capita growth: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (crowding reduces per-capita growth smoothly without explicit carrying capacity term)
- Density-dependent mortality added: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order crowding or interference effects)
- Time-gated intervention (smooth): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (t - c3))) * P - c4 * P**2 (policy/management shift around time c3)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If per-capita growth dP_dt / P is roughly constant in P → favor dP_dt ∝ P (exponential regime).
- If dP_dt increases with P at low P but turns over and becomes negative at high P → include a negative quadratic term (e.g., P - P^2 structure).
- If the approach to a ceiling is more/less abrupt than logistic → use theta-logistic (1 - (c*P)^theta) to tune curvature near carrying capacity.
- If growth slows roughly in proportion to log of size (often linear in log(P)) → include P * log(c*P) (Gompertz-type).
- If there is a minimum viable population (negative growth at low P) → include an Allee factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying the growth term.
- If growth shows periodic rises/falls at fixed timescales → include sinusoidal forcing in the per-capita rate: (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3)) * P.
- If an intervention starts around a particular time and then saturates → use tanh(c*(t-t0)) or similar smooth step in the per-capita rate.
- If removal/harvesting is evident as a roughly constant downward shift in dP_dt → include a constant subtraction term (-c).
- If removal scales with population size (e.g., proportional catchability) → include a -c*P term in addition to intrinsic growth.
- If crowding effects appear sharper at high P than a simple quadratic → add higher-order terms (e.g., -P^3) or use rational saturation P/(1+c*P).

Let \(A=0.7213553457664288\), \(a=6.6511035054181695\), \(b=13.538092585698905\).
GT:
\[
A(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P + A(1-P/b)P + A P^{1/3}.
\]
Combine the first two terms:
\[
A(1-P/b)P\big[(-1+P/a)+1\big] + A P^{1/3}
= A(1-P/b)P\cdot (P/a) + A P^{1/3}.
\]
So
\[
\text{GT} = \frac{A}{a}P^2 - \frac{A}{ab}P^3 + A P^{1/3}.
\]
This is a sum of a cubic polynomial in \(P\) **plus** a fractional power term \(A P^{1/3}\). There is **no** \(t\)-dependence.

Key consequence: any candidate built only from integer-power polynomials, rationals like \(P^k/(1+\alpha P)\), logs, trig, exp, Abs, etc. cannot equal \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\) by choosing constants (unless it explicitly contains a \(P^{c}\) term with a free exponent that can be set to \(1/3\)). Also any unavoidable \(t\)-dependence must be zeroed out.

## GT Analysis

GT: `0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333`

Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511`, `d = 13.538`.

First term: `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
Second term: `a*(1 - P/d)*P`
Third term: `a*P^(1/3)`

Let me combine the first two terms. Factor out `a*(1 - P/d)*P`:
`a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(-1 + P/b) + 1] = a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b)`
`= a*P²/b * (1 - P/d)`
`= a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)`

So GT = `a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d) + a*P^(1/3)`

With numerical values:
- Coefficient of P³: `-a/(b*d) ≈ -0.7214/(6.651*13.538) ≈ -0.008008`
- Coefficient of P²: `a/b ≈ 0.7214/6.651 ≈ 0.10846`
- Plus `a*P^(1/3) ≈ 0.7214*P^(1/3)`

**GT simplified: `c_3*P³ + c_2*P² + c_1*P^(1/3)`** where c_3 < 0, c_2 > 0, c_1 > 0.

The key basis functions are: **P³, P², and P^(1/3)**.

Now I need to check which candidates can produce exactly these three terms (P³, P², P^(1/3)) and nothing else.

The critical issue is the **P^(1/3)** term. Most candidates use rational functions, logarithms, or other forms that cannot exactly equal P^(1/3).

Let me check candidates that might have a P^(1/3) term:

- **Candidate 22**: Has `P**c5*c6` and `P**c7*c8*exp(c9*t)`. Setting c8=0 eliminates the t-dependent term. Then `P**c5*c6` with c5=1/3 gives P^(1/3). Remaining: `P³*c0 + P²*(c1+c2) + P*(c3+c4) + c6*P^(1/3)`. Need P coefficient = 0 (set c3+c4=0). This gives P³ + P² + P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 35**: `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*(P*c4)**c5 + P*c6 + P*c7 + c8`. The term `P*c3*(P*c4)**c5 = c3*c4^c5 * P^(1+c5)`. Set c5 = -2/3, then P^(1/3). Remaining linear P terms: set c2+c6+c7=0, c8=0. This gives P³ + P² + P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 39**: `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3/(P*c4+1) + P + P^c5*c6`. Set c5=1/3 for P^(1/3). The rational term P*c3/(P*c4+1) is not a polynomial - but we can set c3=0. Then remaining: P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*(c2+1) + c6*P^(1/3). Set c2=-1. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 43**: Has `P**c6*c7*exp(c8*t)` - t-dependent, set c7=0. Then no P^(1/3). **NO MATCH**
